## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables position x and velocity v, matching second-order ODE models for (non)linear harmonic oscillators. Typical structures combine restoring forces in x, damping/friction in v, and possible external/parametric forcing as functions of t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring acceleration; sign absorbed into c0)
- Linear viscous damping + stiffness: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (mass-spring-damper in first-order state form)
- Constant bias/tilt: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 (gravity/offset force shifting equilibrium)
- Time-harmonic driving: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (externally driven oscillator)
- Parametric stiffness modulation: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type / parametrically excited oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic Duffing extension: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (stronger nonlinear stiffness)
- Nonlinear (amplitude-dependent) damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (damping increases with displacement amplitude)
- Quadratic/drag-like damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic drag / turbulent-like dissipation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (self-excited negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x| via sign of constants)
- Rayleigh oscillator form: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (self-excited oscillations with velocity-nonlinear damping)
- Liénard-type polynomial model: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x + c3 * x**2) * v (general nonlinear damping depending on x)
- Nonlinear coupling between x and v: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x * v (geometric/constraint-induced coupling)
- State-dependent effective stiffness (rational softening): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x / (c3 + x**2) (restoring force saturates/softens at large |x|)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force → dv_dt dominated by odd-in-x terms (x, x**3, x**5), typically with little/no v dependence; implies near energy conservation.
- Dissipation/friction → terms proportional to v or nonlinear in v (v, v*Abs(v), v**3); these remove energy and shrink oscillation amplitude over time.
- Self-excited limit cycles → “negative damping” at small amplitude but positive at large amplitude, often captured by (c0 + c1 * x**2) * v or c0 * v + c1 * v**3.
- Hardening vs softening spring → sign of cubic stiffness term in x**3 changes whether frequency increases or decreases with amplitude (Duffing behavior).
- External forcing → additive sin(c*t + phi) or cos(c*t + phi) terms in dv_dt; produces resonance peaks and beats when forcing frequency matches natural frequency.
- Parametric excitation → time-periodic coefficient multiplying x (or v), e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x; leads to instability tongues (Mathieu-like behavior).
- Equilibrium shift/tilt → constant term in dv_dt moves the stable fixed point away from x=0, changing symmetry of oscillations.
- Velocity-position coupling (x*v) → indicates non-Cartesian coordinates, constraints, or approximate reduced models where damping depends on configuration.
- Saturation/softening at large amplitude → rational-in-x restoring terms like x/(c + x**2) prevent unbounded acceleration growth and can mimic piecewise stiffness.

\[

\]
Expand terms:
- Velocity part: \(-0.4599146803 v +0.4599146803 v^3 -1.8732905740 v = (-2.3332052543)v + (0.4599146803)v^3\).
- Position/time part: \(-2.4993461666 x(0.0579034145 t+1)-2.4993461666 x = -(2.4993461666\cdot 0.0579034145)\,t\,x - (2.4993461666+2.4993461666)x\).
So GT is exactly a polynomial in \((x,v)\) plus a bilinear term \(t x\):
\[
GT = A\,x + B\,t x + C\,v + D\,v^3
\]
with
- \(D=+0.4599146803\)
- \(C=-2.3332052543\)
- \(A=-4.9986923333\)
- \(B=-(2.4993461666\cdot 0.0579034145)\neq 0\)

Key structural requirement: **a nonzero \(t x\) term** (linear in \(t\), linear in \(x\)), and **no trig/exp/log dependence**.

Now check candidates.

1. \(c0 x + c1 v + c2 v^3 + c3 x\cos(c4 t+c5)+ c6\sin(\cdot)\).

44. Same as 43 plus extra \(v\). Still no \(t x\). ❌

45. Same as 43 plus extra \(x\). Still cosine time dependence; cannot produce \(t x\). ❌

46. Has abs/log in \(v\) and \(x\sin(\cdot)\). Not \(t x\). ❌

47. Has \(x\sin(\log(\cdot))\) time dependence; not \(t x\). ❌

48. Same; no \(t x\). ❌

49. Has \(x^{c5}\sin(\cdot)\); not \(t x\). ❌

50. Has \(x\sin(\log(\cdot))\) plus \(\cos((c8 t+1)^{c9})\). No way to get exact linear \(t x\). ❌

Conclusion: every candidate’s \(t\)-dependence is trig/log/exp (or absent) and **none can generate the required nonzero bilinear term \(B\,t\,x\)** while keeping equality for all real \(t,x,v\). Therefore no parameter choice makes any candidate identical to the GT.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (PO33)
============================================================
GT: -c0*beta*v - mu*(c1 - v**c2)*v - omega0**c3*(gamma*t + c4)*x - omega0**c5*x
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare each candidate to it.

## GT Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
`-0.459914680311301*v*(1 - v**2) - 1.87329057400732*v - 2.49934616662645*x*(0.0579034145056311*t + 1) - 2.49934616662645*x`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.459914680311301*v + 0.459914680311301*v**3`
- `- 1.87329057400732*v`
- `- 2.49934616662645*0.0579034145056311*t*x - 2.49934616662645*x`
- `- 2.49934616662645*x`

Combining terms:
- **v terms**: `(-0.459914680311301 - 1.87329057400732)*v = -2.33320525431862*v`
- **v³ terms**: `0.459914680311301*v**3`
- **x terms**: `(-2.49934616662645 - 2.49934616662645)*x = -4.9986923332529*x`
- **t*x terms**: `-2.49934616662645*0.0579034145056311*t*x = -0.144724968685671*t*x`

So GT = **A*x + B*v + C*v³ + D*t*x** where:
- A ≈ -4.999
- B ≈ -2.333
- C ≈ 0.460
- D ≈ -0.145

The GT is a linear combination of: **x, v, v³, t*x**

Now I need to check which candidates can represent exactly this form.

The key question for each candidate is: can its functional form reduce to `a*x + b*v + c*v³ + d*t*x`?

The term `t*x` is crucial. Many candidates use `x*cos(c4*t + c5)` or `x*sin(c4*log(c5*t+1) + c6)` to approximate the `t*x` term. But these are transcendental functions and cannot exactly equal a linear function of `t*x` for all `t`. Let me verify this carefully.

**Can `x*cos(c4*t + c5)` equal `a*x + d*t*x`?**
This requires `cos(c4*t + c5) = a + d*t` for all t, which is impossible since cosine is bounded and periodic while a linear function is unbounded.

**Can `x*sin(c4*log(c5*t+1) + c6)` equal `a*x + d*t*x`?**
This requires `sin(c4*log(c5*t+1) + c6) = a + d*t` for all t ≥ 0, which is also impossible.

So candidates using only trig/log compositions to capture the `t*x` dependence **cannot** match.

However, some candidates have **multiple terms** involving `t` and `x`. Let me check if combinations can work.

**Candidates with `x*cos(c*t)` (no phase) + `x*cos(c*t + c)` (with phase):**
Using `cos(c*t) = cos(c*t+0)` and `cos(c*t+c) = cos(c*t)cos(c) - sin(c*t)sin(c)`, these combine to give `A*x*cos(c*t) + B*x*sin(c*t)`, which still can't equal `a*x + d*t*x`.

Let me now check each candidate systematically:

**Candidate 1**: `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v**3 + c3*x*cos(c4*t + c5) + c6*sin(c7*t + c8)`
Has basis: x, v, v³, x*cos(αt+β), sin(γt+δ). Cannot produce t*x exactly.
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2**: Extra `exp(c7*x)*sin(c8*t+c9)` — can't reduce to t*x.
Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3**: Uses `x*sin(c4*log(c5*t+1)+c6)` + `sin(c8*t+c9)`. Can't produce t*x.
Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 4**: `c0*x + c1*x*cos(c2*t) + c3*v + c4*v**3 + c5*x**3 + c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(c8*x+c9)`. Set c5=0, c6=0: left with x, x*cos(c2*t), v, v³. Can't produce t*x.
Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 5**: Has `log(c7*exp(c8*x+c9*v)+1)` — softplus, can't reduce.
Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 6**: `c0*x + c1*x + c2*v + c3*v**3 + c4*exp(c5*t)*sin(c6*x+c7)`. Set c4=0: gives (c0+c1)*x + c2*v + c3*v³. Missing t*x.
Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 7**: `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v**3 + c3*x*cos(c4*t+c5) + c6`. Constant c6 extra, but still can't produce t*x.
